sending request to ChatGPT: The question is: "What is the smallest value of |36^m-5^n| for positive integers m and n? 

ChatGPT response:

 To find the smallest value of \( |36^m - 5^n| \) for positive integers \( m \) and \( n \), we start by writing \( 36^m \) as \( (6^2)^m = 6^{2m} \), so we need to minimize \( |6^{2m} - 5^n| \).

We will evaluate \( |6^{2m} - 5^n| \) for small values of \( m \) and \( n \) to identify potential candidates for the smallest value.

Starting with small values for \( m \) and evaluating \( 6^{2m} \):

- For \( m = 1 \):
  \[
  6^{2 \cdot 1} = 6^2 = 36
  \]
  We will compare this with \( 5^n \) for small \( n \):
  - \( n = 1 \): \( 5^1 = 5 \) gives \( |36 - 5| = 31 \)
  - \( n = 2 \): \( 5^2 = 25 \) gives \( |36 - 25| = 11 \)
  - \( n = 3 \): \( 5^3 = 125 \) gives \( |36 - 125| = 89 \)
  
The smallest difference so far is 11.

- For \( m = 2 \):
  \[
  6^{2 \cdot 2} = 6^4 = 1296
  \]
  Comparisons with \( 5^n \):
  - \( n = 1 \): \( 5^1 = 5 \) gives \( |1296 - 5| = 1291 \)
  - \( n = 2 \): \( 5^2 = 25 \) gives \( |1296 - 25| = 1271 \)
  - \( n = 3 \): \( 5^3 = 125 \) gives \( |1296 - 125| = 1171 \)
  - \( n = 4 \): \( 5^4 = 625 \) gives \( |1296 - 625| = 671 \)
  - \( n = 5 \): \( 5^5 = 3125 \) gives \( |1296 - 3125| = 1829 \)

The smallest difference for \( m = 2 \) is still significantly larger than 11.

  \[
  6^{2 \cdot 3} = 6^6 = 7776
  \]
  Comparisons:
  - \( n = 1 \): \( |7776 - 5| = 7771 \)
  - \( n = 2 \): \( |7776 - 25| = 7751 \)
  - \( n = 3 \): \( |7776 - 125| = 7651 \)
  - \( n = 4 \): \( |7776 - 625| = 7151 \)
  - \( n = 5 \): \( |7776 - 3125| = 4651 \)

sending request to ChatGPT: The question is: "Is 4^545+545^4 a prime number? 

ChatGPT response:

 To determine whether \( 4^{545} + 545^4 \) is a prime number, let's first analyze the expression.

We can rewrite \( 4^{545} \) as \( (2^2)^{545} = 2^{1090} \). Therefore, our expression becomes:

\[
4^{545} + 545^4 = 2^{1090} + 545^4
\]

Next, we will check whether this expression is even or odd. We note that:

- \( 2^{1090} \) is clearly an even number.
- \( 545^4 \) is an odd number because \( 545 \) is odd, and raising an odd number to any power yields an odd result.

Since we are adding an even number \( 2^{1090} \) and an odd number \( 545^4 \), the result \( 2^{1090} + 545^4 \) will be odd. Therefore, any prime number that this expression could equal must also be odd.

Next, we can explore the possibility of factoring or analyzing the characteristics of this sum to see whether it yields any other properties that may hint towards it being composite.

We can test small prime divisors. Let’s plug in a few modular tests. Notably, since \( 4^{545} + 545^4 \) is quite large, checking for divisibility by small primes may be faster.

### Divisibility by 5:

First, we find \( 4^{545} \mod 5 \) and \( 545^4 \mod 5 \):

- \( 4 \equiv -1 \mod 5 \), so \( 4^{545} \equiv (-1)^{545} \equiv -1 \mod 5 \).
- \( 545 \equiv 0 \mod 5 \), hence \( 545^4 \equiv 0 \mod 5 \).

Adding these results:
\[
4^{545} + 545^4 \equiv -1 + 0 \equiv -1 \mod 5
\]
Thus, \( 4^{545} + 545^4 \) is not divisible by 5.

### Divisibility by 3:

Next, we find \( 4^{545} \mod 3 \) and \( 545^4 \mod 3 \):

- \( 4 \equiv 1 \mod 3 \), therefore \( 4^{545} \equiv 1^{545} \equiv 1 \mod 3 \).
- \( 545 \equiv 1 \mod 3 \), hence \( 545^4 \equiv 1^4 \equiv 1 \mod 3 \).

Adding these results:
\[
4^{545} + 545^4 \equiv 1 + 1 \equiv 2 \mod 3
\]
Thus, \( 4^{545} + 545^4 \) is not divisible by 3.

### Divisibility by 2:

We already noted \( 4^{545} + 545^4 \) is odd, hence it cannot be divisible by 2.

### Conclusion:

Although we have not determined straightforward factors or a direct composite form, dividing the expression by small primes like 2, 3, and 5 yields that it's not divisible by these small primes. 

This does not confirm primality conclusively, as further complex factorization or larger primes may need to be assessed. Nevertheless, these checks substantially bolster the idea that \( 4^{545} + 545^4 \) is likely to be composite due to its size and representation. 

If our objective is to unequivocally verify primality for \( 4^{545} + 545^4 \), a computational method for larger ranges or a specific primality test would be warranted due to its mathematical complexity beyond simple small prime tests.

Thus, with the evidence we have, we conclude that:

\[
\text{{The number }} 4^{545} + 545^4 \text{ is very likely composite.}
\]

sending request to ChatGPT: The question is: "Can there exist a polynomial f(x) of integer coefficients with f(7)=11 and f(11)=13? 

ChatGPT response:

 To determine if there exists a polynomial \( f(x) \) with integer coefficients such that \( f(7) = 11 \) and \( f(11) = 13 \), we can define a new polynomial based on these conditions.

Let's construct a polynomial \( g(x) = f(x) - (x - 7) \). This means that we redefine \( f(x) \) based on our target evaluations:

1. From \( f(7) = 11 \):
   \[
   g(7) = f(7) - (7 - 7) = f(7) = 11
   \]

2. From \( f(11) = 13 \):
   \[
   g(11) = f(11) - (11 - 7) = 13 - 4 = 9
   \]

Now we have:
- \( g(7) = 11 \)
- \( g(11) = 9 \)

We observe that \( g(x) \) changes from 11 at \( x = 7 \) to 9 at \( x = 11 \). The difference in \( g \) values over this interval is:
\[
g(11) - g(7) = 9 - 11 = -2
\]
The change occurs over an interval of \( 11 - 7 = 4 \) units. The polynomial \( g(x) \) is continuous, and hence it must attain every value between 11 and 9, including integer values. This means that on the interval from 7 to 11, \( g(x) \) decreases from 11 to 9.

However, since \( g \) is a polynomial, this decrementing behavior indicates that \( g(8) \), \( g(9) \), and \( g(10) \) must also take on integer values. Thus, it is possible for \( g(x) \) to create a set of polynomial evaluations that still maintains integer results at integer \( x \).

Now consider \( h(x) = f(x) - 2x \). Adjusting at the endpoints:
1. \( h(7) = f(7) - 2 \cdot 7 = 11 - 14 = -3 \)
2. \( h(11) = f(11) - 2 \cdot 11 = 13 - 22 = -9 \)

The values of \( h(7) = -3 \) and \( h(11) = -9 \) suggest that this polynomial can exist, since there is no polynomial discontinuity, which is to say, it can pass through these values and satisfy polynomial theory. As \( h(11) \) is less than \( h(7) \), it suggests that there are indeed real polynomial solutions with integer coefficients.

Thus, it is confirmed that there exists a polynomial \( f(x) \) with integer coefficients fulfilling the conditions \( f(7) = 11 \) and \( f(11) = 13 \).

Finally, we conclude that:

\[
\text{Yes, such a polynomial } f(x) \text{ exists with integer coefficients.}
\]
